## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics (classical mechanics: nonlinear oscillators)
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is acceleration, with state variables x (position) and v (velocity) evolving in time t, matching second-order ODE models of (non)linear harmonic oscillators. Typical structures include restoring forces from potentials (often nonlinear in x), damping (linear or nonlinear in v), and optional external/parametric forcing in t.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear harmonic oscillator (Hooke restoring force): dv_dt = c0 * x (small oscillations about equilibrium; sign absorbed into c0)
- Linear viscous damping + linear spring: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (damped oscillator; c1 typically negative)
- Constant bias / gravity / offset acceleration: dv_dt = c0 + c1 * x + c2 * v (equilibrium shifted or constant background acceleration)
- Duffing oscillator (cubic stiffness): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (hardening/softening spring with damping)
- Quintic stiffness extension: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 + c3 * v (stronger nonlinear restoring force)
- Pendulum (sine restoring force): dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) + c2 * v (large-angle oscillations; c1 rescales x to an angle)
- Polynomial restoring force as gradient of a potential: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 + c3 * v (generic asymmetric potential near equilibrium)
- Van der Pol–type nonlinear damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + (c1 + c2 * x**2) * v (self-excited oscillations when damping changes sign with amplitude)
- Quadratic/cubic drag damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v * Abs(v) (or c2 * v**3) (nonlinear dissipation)
- Duffing with harmonic driving: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (externally driven nonlinear resonance)
- Parametric excitation (time-varying stiffness): dv_dt = (c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x + c3 * v (Mathieu-type parametric resonance)
- State-dependent frequency (amplitude-dependent stiffness in trigonometric form): dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) + c2 * x**3 + c3 * v (hybrid pendulum/Duffing behavior)
- Coupled state forcing term: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * x * v (nonlinear coupling from geometric or velocity-position interaction)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Conservative restoring force from a potential: dv_dt often equals -dU/dx, so polynomial U(x) implies dv_dt as a polynomial in x (odd powers for symmetric potentials).
- Energy dissipation: terms proportional to v reduce mechanical energy; nonlinear drag commonly appears as v*Abs(v) or v**3 rather than purely linear v.
- Amplitude-dependent frequency: adding x**3 (Duffing) or sin(c*x) makes oscillation frequency depend on amplitude, producing backbone curves in resonance.
- Self-excitation/limit cycles: damping that depends on x (e.g., (c0+c1*x**2)*v) can be negative at small amplitude and positive at large amplitude, yielding stable limit cycles.
- External periodic forcing: additive cos(c*t) or sin(c*t) terms create driven resonance, entrainment, and possibly chaos when combined with nonlinearity.
- Parametric resonance signature: multiplicative time dependence on x (e.g., (c0+c1*cos(c*t))*x) indicates stiffness modulation rather than additive forcing.
- Asymmetry in the restoring force: even powers of x (x**2, x**4) or mixed terms shift equilibrium and produce different behavior for +x vs -x.
- Non-smooth/friction-like effects: presence of Abs(v) or sign-like structures typically models dry friction or quadratic drag, causing sharp transitions near v=0.

============================================================
GT Equivalence Verification (PO22)
============================================================
GT: -c0*beta*v - beta*exp(-Abs(x))*v - mu*(c1 - x**c2)*v - omega0**c3*x**c4
Candidate formulas: 65

GT (fully numeric) is
\[
-0.752289977167006\,v(1-x^2)\;-\;0.61401597703647\,v\;-\;0.307007988518235\,v\,e^{-|x|}\;-\;1.1598282332023\,x^3.
\]
Rewrite the polynomial-in-\(v\) part:
\[
-0.752289977167006\,v(1-x^2)= -0.752289977167006\,v +0.752289977167006\,v x^2.
\]
So GT is exactly of the form
\[
(\text{const})\,v + (\text{const})\,v x^2 + (\text{const})\,x^3 + (\text{const})\,v e^{-|x|},
\]
with **no** dependence on \(t\), no constant offset, no other nonlinearities, and crucially the exponential is \(e^{-|x|}\) (absolute value in the exponent with a negative sign).

Thus any candidate can match only if it can be reduced (by setting free constants) to
\[
c_0 v + c_1 v x^2 + c_2 x^3 + c_3 v e^{c_4|x|}
\]
with \(c_4=-1\), and all extra terms set to 0.

---

### Candidate-by-candidate analysis

1. \(c0*v + c1*v*x^2 + c2*x^3 + c3*v*exp(c4*Abs(x)) + c5*\log(\cdots)\)  
   Set \(c5=0\) to remove the log term. Then choose
   - \(c4=-1\) to get \(e^{-|x|}\),
   - \(c3=-0.307007988518235\),
   - \(c2=-1.1598282332023\),
   - \(c1=+0.752289977167006\),
   - \(c0=-(0.752289977167006+0.61401597703647)=-1.366305954203476\).
   This matches GT exactly. ✅ **Match**

2. Has \(v\log(c4|x|+1)\) and \(v e^{c6 x}\) (no \(|x|\) in exponent). You can zero out one/both via \(c3=0,c5=0\), but then you cannot produce the required \(v e^{-|x|}\) term. ❌

3. Has \(v e^{c4 x}\) (no \(|x|\)) and extra \(c5 + c6 e^{c7 t}\). You can set \(c5=0,c6=0\), but still cannot make \(e^{-|x|}\) for all \(x\). ❌

4. Includes \(c0*x\) and a \(\log(\,|v|\,)\) term; cannot generate \(v e^{-|x|}\) and must kill extra terms; even after killing, remaining structure doesn’t include \(v e^{-|x|}\). ❌

5. Like (3) plus trig \(x\cos(c7 x)\cos(c8 t)\). Can zero trig term, but still only \(e^{c4 x}\) not \(e^{-|x|}\). ❌

6. Like (3) plus linear \(x\). Can zero extras, still wrong exponential. ❌

7. Has \(c4 v e^{c5 x}\) (no \(|x|\)) and an \(\mathrm{Abs}(x)\) additive term; cannot form \(v e^{-|x|}\). ❌

8. Has \(v e^{c4 x}\) and a softplus-like \(\log(c6 e^{c7 x}+1)\); can zero log term but still wrong exponential. ❌

9. Has extra \(x^2\) term; can set \(c6=0,c5=0\), but still wrong exponential \(e^{c4 x}\). ❌

10. Has \(v e^{c4 x}\) and \(x\sin(\cdot t)\); can set trig coefficient 0, but still wrong exponential. ❌

    Exactly the needed template; set \(c4=-1\) and match coefficients. ✅ **Match**

34. Uses \(\mathrm{Abs}(v)\) multiplying \(e^{c4 x}\); GT is linear in \(v\) (sign-sensitive), so cannot match globally. ❌

35. Has \(v e^{c3 x}\) (no \(|x|\)) plus duplicated \(v\) terms; cannot produce \(e^{-|x|}\). ❌

47. Has \(v e^{c4 x}\) and \(v x^4\); can zero extra but exponential wrong. ❌

48. Contains \(x^{c4}e^{c5 x}\) and \(v e^{c7|x|}\) but also an \(x\) term; you could set \(c0=0\) and kill the \(x^{c4}e^{c5 x}\) term via \(c3=0\). Then you have \(c1 v + c2 v x^2 + c6 v e^{c7|x|}\), but you still need the \(-1.1598 x^3\) term, which is impossible after setting \(c3=0\). If you keep \(c3\neq 0\) to make \(x^3\), it is multiplied by \(e^{c5 x}\), which cannot equal a pure \(x^3\) globally unless \(c5=0\) and \(c4=3\); but then the term is \(c3 x^3\) (good). However the same \(c3\) term would be \(c3 x^3 e^{0}=c3 x^3\) (ok). Then you can set \(c7=-1\) and match \(v e^{-|x|}\). Also set \(c0=0\) to remove linear \(x\). This actually can match: choose \(c4=3,c5=0,c3=-1.1598282332023\), and match \(v\), \(v x^2\), \(v e^{-|x|}\) via \(c1,c2,c6,c7=-1\). ✅ **Match**
